<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color:#b0c4de">Douyin (TikTok)</th></tr><tr style="display:none;"><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a></th><td><span lang="zh-Hani" style="font-size:1rem;" title="Chinese language text">抖音</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;">Literal meaning</th><td>"vibrating sound"</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><table class="collapsible collapsed" style="padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size: 100%; text-align: left; background-color: #f9ffbc;">Transcriptions</th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcffc9;"><a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">Standard Mandarin</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Hanyu_Pinyin" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanyu Pinyin">Hanyu Pinyin</a></th><td><span style="font-style:normal" lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language romanization">Dǒuyīn</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Mandarin" title="Help:IPA/Mandarin">IPA</a></th><td><span style="font-style:normal" lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language romanization"><span class="IPA" style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Mandarin" title="Help:IPA/Mandarin">[to&#768;u.i&#769;n]</a></span></span></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>TikTok</b> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">抖音</span>; Dǒuyīn) is a Chinese <a href="/wiki/Online_video_platform" title="Online video platform">video-sharing</a> <a href="/wiki/Social_networking_service" title="Social networking service">social networking service</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/ByteDance" title="ByteDance">ByteDance</a>, a Beijing-based company founded in 2012 by <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Yiming" title="Zhang Yiming">Zhang Yiming</a>. It is used to create short dance, lip-sync, comedy and talent videos.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> ByteDance first launched <b>Douyin</b> for the China market in September 2016. Later, TikTok  was launched in 2017 for <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> in markets outside of China. It became available in the United States after merging with <a href="/wiki/Musical.ly" title="Musical.ly">musical.ly</a> on 2 August 2018. TikTok and Douyin are similar to each other and essentially  the same app, however they run on separate servers to comply with <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_China" title="Internet censorship in China">Chinese censorship restrictions</a>. The application allows users to create short music and <a href="/wiki/Lip_sync" title="Lip sync">lip-sync</a> videos of 3 to 15 seconds<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and short looping videos of 3 to 60 seconds. The app is popular in Asia, the United States, and other parts of the world. TikTok and Douyin's servers are based in countries where the apps are available.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After merging with musical.ly in August, downloads rose and TikTok became the most downloaded app in the US in October 2018, the first Chinese app to achieve this.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> As of 2018, it was available in over 150 markets and in 75 languages. In February 2019, TikTok, together with Douyin, hit one billion downloads globally, excluding Android installs in China.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, media outlets cited TikTok as the 7th-most-downloaded mobile app of the decade, from 2010 to 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> It was also the most-downloaded app on the <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(iOS)" title="App Store (iOS)">App Store</a> in 2018 and 2019.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution">Evolution</span></h3>
<p>Douyin was launched by ByteDance in China in September 2016, originally under the name A.me, before rebranding to Douyin in December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Douyin was developed in 200 days and within a year had 100 million users, with more than one billion videos viewed every day.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> TikTok was launched in the international market in September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On 23 January 2018, the TikTok app ranked No. 1 among free app downloads on app stores in Thailand and other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>TikTok has been downloaded about 80 million times in the United States, and 800 million times worldwide, according to data from mobile research firm Sensor Tower that excludes Android users in China.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Many celebrities including <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Fallon" title="Jimmy Fallon">Jimmy Fallon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Hawk" title="Tony Hawk">Tony Hawk</a> began using the application in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 September 2019, TikTok and the US <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL) announced a multi-year partnership.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The agreement occurred just two days shy of the NFL's 100th season kick off at the Soldier stadium, where TikTok hosted activities for fans in honor of the deal. The partnership entails the launch of an official NFL TikTok account which will bring about new marketing opportunities such as sponsored videos and hashtag challenges.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical.ly_merger">Musical.ly merger</span></h3>
<p>On 9 November 2017, TikTok's parent company, ByteDance, spent up to $1 billion to purchase <a href="/wiki/Musical.ly" title="Musical.ly">musical.ly</a>, a startup based in Shanghai with an office in Santa Monica, California.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BusinessInsider_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusinessInsider-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Musical.ly was a social media video platform that allowed users to create short lip-sync and comedy videos. Its official release was in August 2014. Looking forward to leveraging the US digital platform's young user base, TikTok merged with musical.ly on 2 August 2018 to create a larger video community, with existing accounts and data consolidated into one app, keeping the title TikTok. This ended musical.ly and made TikTok a world-wide app, excluding China.<sup id="cite_ref-BusinessInsider_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusinessInsider-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_in_other_markets">Expansion in other markets</span></h3>
<p>As of 2018, TikTok has been made available in over 150 markets, and in 75 languages.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> TikTok was downloaded more than 104 million times on Apple's App store during the full first half of 2018, according to data provided to CNBC by Sensor Tower. It surpassed <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> and <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> to become the world's most downloaded iOS app.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Douyin">Douyin</span></h3>
<p>As a separate app from TikTok, Douyin is available from the developer's website. Part of its popularity is attributable to its marketing campaigns, launching several activities with Chinese celebrities to engage their fans' interest. For example, its marketing campaign in 2018 Spring Festival Gala alone brought an increase of 70 million daily active users.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In February 2018, Douyin launched a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Modern_Sky" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern Sky">Modern Sky</a> to monetize music.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Features">Features</span></h2>
<p>The TikTok mobile app allows users to create a short video of themselves which often feature music in the background, can be sped up, slowed down or edited with a filter.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> To create a music video with the app, users can choose background music from a wide variety of <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">music genres</a>, edit with a filter and record a 15-second video with speed adjustments before uploading it to share with others on TikTok or other social platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> They can also film short lip-sync videos to popular songs.
</p><p>The app's "react" feature allows users to film their reaction to a specific video, over which it is placed in a small window that is movable around the screen.<sup id="cite_ref-TechCrunch_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TechCrunch-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Its "duet" feature allows users to film a video aside another video.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The “duet” feature was another trademark of Musical.ly.
</p><p>The app allows users to set their accounts as "private." Private content remains visible to TikTok, but is blocked from TikTok users who the account holder has not authorized to view their content.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Users can choose whether any other user, or only their "friends", may interact with them through the app via comments, messages, or "react" or "duet" videos.<sup id="cite_ref-TechCrunch_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TechCrunch-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Users also can set specific videos to either “public”, “friends only”, or “private” regardless if the account is private or not.
</p><p>The “for you” page on TikTok is a feed of videos that are recommended to users based on their activity on the app. Content is generated by TikTok depending on what kind of content a user liked, interacted with, or searched. Users can only be featured on the “for you” page if they are 16 or over as per TikTok policy. Users under 16 will not show up under the “for you” page, the sounds page, or under any hashtags.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Users can also add videos, hashtags, filters, and sounds to their “saved” section. This section is visible only to the user on their profile allowing them to refer back to any video, hashtag, filter, or sound they've previously saved.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Artificial_intelligence">Artificial intelligence</span></h3>
<p>TikTok employs artificial intelligence to analyze users' interests and preferences through their interactions with the content, and display a personalized content feed for each user.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="User_characteristics_and_behavior">User characteristics and behavior</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Users">Users</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_most-followed_TikTok_accounts" title="List of most-followed TikTok accounts">List of most-followed TikTok accounts</a></div>
<p>In the three years after it launched on September 2016, TikTok acquired 800 million active users.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h4>
<p>In the United States, 52% of TikTok users are iPhone users. While TikTok has a neutral gender-bias format, 44% of TikTok users are female while 56% are male.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> TikTok's geographical use has shown that 43% of new users are from India.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> TikTok has proven to attract the younger generation, as 41% of its users are between the ages of 16 and 24. Among these TikTok users, 90% say they use the app on a daily basis.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="User_engagement">User engagement</span></h3>
<p>TikTok's user engagement rate is 29%. As of July 2018, TikTok users spend an average of 52 minutes a day on the app. ByteDance has stated that U.S. users open the app eight times a day and individual sessions on the app are the longest at 4.9 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Viral_trends">Viral trends</span></h3>
<p>There are a variety of trends within TikTok, including <a href="/wiki/Internet_meme" title="Internet meme">memes</a>, lip-synced songs, and comedy videos. Duets, a feature that allows users to add their own video to an existing video with the original content's audio, have sparked most of these trends.
</p><p>Trends are shown on TikTok's explore page or the page with the search logo. The page enlists the trending <a href="/wiki/Hashtag" title="Hashtag">hashtags</a> and challenges among the app. Some include #posechallenge, #filterswitch, #makeeverysecondcount, #wannalisten, #pillowchallenge, #furrywar, #hitormiss, #bottlecapchallenge and more. In June 2019, the company introduced the hash tag #EduTok which received 37 billion views. Following this development the company initiated partnerships with <a href="/wiki/EdTech" class="mw-redirect" title="EdTech">edtech</a> start ups to create educational content on the platform.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The app has spawned numerous <a href="/wiki/Viral_phenomenon" title="Viral phenomenon">viral trends</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_celebrity" title="Internet celebrity">internet celebrities</a>, and music trends around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charli_D%27Amelio" title="Charli D&#39;Amelio">Charli D'Amelio</a> is currently the most followed TikTok user with more than 50 million followers.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>  Having not been previously famous before becoming a user on the app, Charli rose to fame after a dance tutorial she posted in July 2019 went viral. She is also well known for a video of her performing a dance called "The Renegade," to the song "Lottery" by <a href="/wiki/K_Camp" title="K Camp">K CAMP</a>. Other TikTok stars like <a href="/wiki/Loren_Gray" title="Loren Gray">Loren Gray</a>, have maintained fame over the years after initially going viral on Musical.ly. Studies have shown that in just one year, short videos in China have gone up by 94.79 million.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Aside from "The Renegade," another notable TikTok meme is "hit or miss", from a snippet of iLOVEFRiDAY's "<a href="/wiki/Mia_Khalifa_(Diss)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mia Khalifa (Diss)">Mia Khalifa</a>" (2018), which has been used in over four million TikTok videos, and helped introduce the app to a larger Western audience.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Other songs that have gained popularity because of their success on the app include "<a href="/wiki/Roxanne_(Arizona_Zervas_song)" title="Roxanne (Arizona Zervas song)">Roxanne</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Zervas" title="Arizona Zervas">Arizona Zervas</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Lalala_(song)" title="Lalala (song)">Lalala</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Bbno$" title="Bbno$">bbno$</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Stupid_(Ashnikko_song)" title="Stupid (Ashnikko song)">Stupid</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Ashnikko" title="Ashnikko">Ashnikko</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Yellow_Hearts" title="Yellow Hearts">Yellow Hearts</a>" by Ant Saunders, "<a href="/wiki/Truth_Hurts_(song)" title="Truth Hurts (song)">Truth Hurts</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Lizzo" title="Lizzo">Lizzo</a> and a remix of <a href="/wiki/Jay_Sean" title="Jay Sean">Jay Sean</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Ride_It_(Jay_Sean_song)" title="Ride It (Jay Sean song)">Ride It</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Regard_(DJ)" title="Regard (DJ)">Regard</a>. TikTok was a major factor in making "<a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Road" title="Old Town Road">Old Town Road</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Lil_Nas_X" title="Lil Nas X">Lil Nas X</a> become one of the biggest songs of 2019, and the longest running #1 song on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Billboard Hot 100</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>TikTok has allowed bands to get notoriety in places all around the globe. The band <a href="/wiki/Fitz_and_The_Tantrums" title="Fitz and The Tantrums">Fitz and The Tantrums</a> has developed a large following in South Korea despite never having toured in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> After his song "Old Town Road" went viral on the app, Lil Nas X received a record deal and the song rose to the top of the Billboard charts. The platform has received some criticism for its lack of royalties towards artists whose music is used on their platform.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> There is controversy over whether or not this type of promotion is beneficial in the long run for artists.
</p><p>TikTok has increased popularity in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> since February 2020, specifically during the ongoing <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, with several people dancing on the video itself.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h2>
<p>TikTok became the world's most downloaded app on Apple's App Store in the first half of 2018 with an estimated 104 million downloads in that time.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Studies have shown that in just one year, short videos in China have gone up by 94.79 million.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cyberbullying_and_addiction_concerns">Cyberbullying and addiction concerns</span></h3>
<p>Similar to other platforms,<sup id="cite_ref-2018-11-16-cnetfr_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-11-16-cnetfr-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> journalists in several countries have raised privacy concerns about the app, because it is popular with children and has the potential to be used by sexual predators.<sup id="cite_ref-2018-11-16-cnetfr_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-11-16-cnetfr-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several users have reported endemic cyberbullying on TikTok,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> including racism.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In December 2019, following a report by German digital rights group <a href="/wiki/Netzpolitik.org" title="Netzpolitik.org">Netzpolitik.org</a>, TikTok admitted that it had suppressed videos by disabled users as well as LGBTQ users in a purported effort to limit cyberbullying.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theintercept_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theintercept-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition, some users may find it hard to stop using TikTok.<sup id="cite_ref-scmp_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scmp-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> In April 2018, an addiction-reduction feature was added to Douyin.<sup id="cite_ref-scmp_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scmp-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> This encouraged users to take a break every 90 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-scmp_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scmp-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>  Later in 2018, the feature was rolled out to the TikTok app.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="User_privacy_concerns">User privacy concerns</span></h3>
<p>Privacy concerns have also been brought up regarding the app.<sup id="cite_ref-Wong2019_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wong2019-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In its privacy policy, TikTok lists that it collects usage information, IP addresses, a user's mobile carrier, unique device identifiers, keystroke patterns, and location data, among other data.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahadevan2020_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahadevan2020-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PrivacyPolicy_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrivacyPolicy-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2020, Check Point Research discovered a security flaw in TikTok which could have allowed hackers access to user accounts using SMS.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In February, <a href="/wiki/Reddit" title="Reddit">Reddit</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Steve_Huffman" title="Steve Huffman">Steve Huffman</a> criticised the app, calling it "spyware," and stating "I look at that app as so fundamentally parasitic, that it's always listening, the fingerprinting technology they use is truly terrifying, and I could not bring myself to install an app like that on my phone."<sup id="cite_ref-Hamilton2020_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamilton2020-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Responding to Huffman's comments, TikTok stated "These are baseless accusations made without a shred of evidence."<sup id="cite_ref-Mahadevan2020_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahadevan2020-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Data_Protection_Authority" title="Dutch Data Protection Authority">Dutch Data Protection Authority</a> announced an investigation into TikTok in relation to privacy protections for children.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_security_concerns">National security concerns</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_intelligence_activity_abroad" title="Chinese intelligence activity abroad">Chinese intelligence activity abroad</a></div>
<p>In January 2019, an investigation by the American think tank <a href="/wiki/Peterson_Institute_for_International_Economics" title="Peterson Institute for International Economics">Peterson Institute for International Economics</a> described TikTok as a "Huawei-sized problem" that posed a national security threat to the West,<sup id="cite_ref-2019-01-11-piie_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019-01-11-piie-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2019-01-14-twnews_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019-01-14-twnews-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> noting the app's popularity with Western users. They included armed forces personnel and its alleged ability to convey location, image and biometric data to its Chinese parent company, which is legally unable to refuse to share data with the Chinese government under the <a href="/wiki/China_Internet_Security_Law" title="China Internet Security Law">China Internet Security Law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2019-01-14-twnews_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019-01-14-twnews-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Observers have also noted that ByteDance's founder and CEO Zhang Yiming issued a letter in 2018 stating that his company would "further deepen cooperation" with <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party of China</a> authorities to promote their policies.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> TikTok's parent company ByteDance claims that TikTok is not available in China and its data is stored outside of China, but its privacy policy has reserved the right to share any information with Chinese authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In response to national security, censorship, and <a href="/wiki/Anti-boycott" title="Anti-boycott">anti-boycott</a> compliance concerns, in October 2019, Senator <a href="/wiki/Marco_Rubio" title="Marco Rubio">Marco Rubio</a> asked the <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Foreign_Investment_in_the_United_States" title="Committee on Foreign Investment in the United States">Committee on Foreign Investment in the United States</a> to open an investigation into TikTok and its parent company ByteDance.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The same month, senators <a href="/wiki/Tom_Cotton" title="Tom Cotton">Tom Cotton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Schumer" title="Chuck Schumer">Chuck Schumer</a> sent a joint letter to the <a href="/wiki/Director_of_National_Intelligence" title="Director of National Intelligence">Director of National Intelligence</a> requesting a security review of TikTok and its parent company.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2019, it was reported that the Committee on Foreign Investment in the United States opened an investigation into ByteDance's acquisition of Musical.ly.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The same month, following a request by Senator Chuck Schumer, U.S. Army Secretary <a href="/wiki/Ryan_McCarthy_(U.S._Army)" title="Ryan McCarthy (U.S. Army)">Ryan McCarthy</a> agreed to assess the risks of using TikTok as a recruitment tool.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Senator <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hawley" title="Josh Hawley">Josh Hawley</a> introduced the National Security and Personal Data Protection Act to prohibit TikTok's parent company and others from transferring personal data of Americans to China.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In December 2019, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">U.S. Army</a> banned TikTok from all government-issued devices.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Transportation_Security_Administration" title="Transportation Security Administration">Transportation Security Administration</a> also prohibited its personnel from posting on the platform for outreach purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Following its prohibition by the U.S. military, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Defence_Force" title="Australian Defence Force">Australian Defence Force</a> also banned TikTok on its devices.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Legislation was subsequently introduced in the U.S. Senate that would prohibit all federal employees from using or downloading TikTok.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Censorship">Censorship</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Overseas_censorship_of_Chinese_issues" title="Overseas censorship of Chinese issues">Overseas censorship of Chinese issues</a></div>
<p>On 3 July 2018, TikTok was banned in Indonesia, after the Indonesian government accused it of promulgating "pornography, inappropriate content and blasphemy."<sup id="cite_ref-2018-07-11-st_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-07-11-st-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2018-07-05-reuters_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-07-05-reuters-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2018-07-05-dw_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-07-05-dw-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:3_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2018-12-19-tc_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-12-19-tc-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Shortly afterwards, TikTok pledged to task 20 staff with censoring TikTok content in Indonesia,<sup id="cite_ref-2018-07-05-reuters_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-07-05-reuters-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> and the ban was lifted 8 days later.<sup id="cite_ref-2018-07-11-st_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-07-11-st-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2018, the Bangladeshi government blocked the TikTok app's internet access.<sup id="cite_ref-2019-02-25-dw_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019-02-25-dw-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also in 2018, Douyin was reprimanded by Chinese media watchdogs for showing "unacceptable" content, such as videos depicting adolescent pregnancies.<sup id="cite_ref-2018-12-19-tc_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-12-19-tc-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2019, the Chinese government said that it would start to hold app developers like ByteDance responsible for user content shared via apps such as Douyin,<sup id="cite_ref-2019-01-14-metro_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019-01-14-metro-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and listed 100 types of content that the Chinese government would censor.<sup id="cite_ref-2019-01-18-variety_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019-01-18-variety-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> It was reported that certain content unfavorable to the Communist Party of China has already been limited for users outside of China such as content related to the <a href="/wiki/2019_Hong_Kong_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2019 Hong Kong protests">2019 Hong Kong protests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> TikTok has blocked videos about <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_China" title="Human rights in China">human rights in China</a>, particularly those that reference <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_re-education_camps" title="Xinjiang re-education camps">Xinjiang re-education camps</a> and abuses of ethnic and religious minorities, and disabled the accounts of users who post them.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> TikTok's policies also ban content related to a specific list of foreign leaders such as <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Its policies also ban content critical of <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdoğan</a> and content considered pro-<a href="/wiki/Kurdish_nationalism" title="Kurdish nationalism">Kurdish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> TikTok was reported to have censored users supportive of the <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_Amendment_Act_protests" title="Citizenship Amendment Act protests">Citizenship Amendment Act protests</a> and those who promote Hindu-Muslim unity.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2019, several Indian politicians called for TikTok to be banned or more tightly regulated, after concerns emerged about sexually explicit content, cyberbullying, and <a href="/wiki/Deepfake" title="Deepfake">deepfakes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In countries where LGBT discrimination is the socio-political norm, TikTok moderators have blocked content that could be perceived as being positive towards LGBT people or LGBT rights, including same-sex couples holding hands, including in countries where homosexuality has never been illegal<sup id="cite_ref-:4_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Former U.S. employees of TikTok reported to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> that final decisions to remove content were made by parent company employees in Beijing.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In response to censorship concerns, TikTok's parent company hired <a href="/wiki/K%26L_Gates" title="K&amp;L Gates">K&amp;L Gates</a>, including former Congressmen <a href="/wiki/Bart_Gordon" title="Bart Gordon">Bart Gordon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Denham" title="Jeff Denham">Jeff Denham</a>, to advise it on its content moderation policies.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> TikTok also hired lobbying firm Monument Advocacy.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, TikTok removed about two dozen accounts that were responsible of posting <a href="/wiki/Use_of_social_media_by_the_Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Use of social media by the Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">ISIS propaganda</a> on the app.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 November 2019, TikTok temporarily suspended the account of 17-year-old Afghan-American user Feroza Aziz after she posted a video, disguised as a makeup tutorial, drawing attention to the internment camps of Muslim <a href="/wiki/Uyghurs" title="Uyghurs">Uyghurs</a> in <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>, China.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> TikTok later claimed that her account was suspended as a result of human error, and her account has since been reinstated.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2020, internal documents leaked to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Intercept" title="The Intercept">The Intercept</a></i> revealed that moderators had been instructed to suppress posts created by users deemed "too ugly, poor, or disabled" for the platform, and to censor political speech in livestreams, punishing those who harmed “national honor" or broadcast streams about "state organs such as police" with bans from the platform.<sup id="cite_ref-theintercept_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theintercept-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2020, it's reported that Douyin suspended users who speak <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a> on its livestreaming platform. In a statement, Bytedance said Douyin is “building out content safety capabilities” and that Cantonese is not “fully supported.” But Bytedance did not explain why.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesian_block">Indonesian block</span></h3>
<p>Indonesia temporarily blocked the TikTok app on 3 July 2018 amid public concern about illegal content such as <a href="/wiki/Pornography" title="Pornography">pornography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blasphemy_law_in_Indonesia" title="Blasphemy law in Indonesia">blasphemy</a>. The app was unblocked one week later after making various changes, including removing negative content, opening a government liaison office, and implementing age restrictions as well as security mechanisms.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tencent_lawsuits">Tencent lawsuits</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tencent" title="Tencent">Tencent</a>'s <a href="/wiki/WeChat" title="WeChat">WeChat</a> platform has been accused of blocking Douyin's videos.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In April 2018, Douyin sued Tencent and accused it of spreading false and damaging information on its WeChat platform, demanding <a href="/wiki/CNY" class="mw-redirect" title="CNY">CNY</a> one million in compensation and an apology. In June 2018, Tencent filed a lawsuit against <a href="/wiki/Toutiao" title="Toutiao">Toutiao</a> and Douyin in a Beijing court, alleging they had repeatedly defamed Tencent with negative news and damaged its reputation, seeking a nominal sum of CNY 1 in compensation and a public apology.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In response, Toutiao filed a complaint the following day against Tencent for allegedly <a href="/wiki/Unfair_competition" title="Unfair competition">unfair competition</a> and asking for CNY 90 million in economic losses.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="US_COPPA_fines">US COPPA fines</span></h3>
<p>On 27 February 2019, the United States <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a> fined ByteDance US $5.7 million for collecting information from minors under the age of 13 in violation of the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Online_Privacy_Protection_Act" title="Children&#39;s Online Privacy Protection Act">Children's Online Privacy Protection Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> ByteDance responded by adding a kids-only mode to TikTok which blocks the upload of videos, the building of user profiles, direct messaging, and commenting on other's videos, while still allowing the viewing and recording of content.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brief_ban_in_India">Brief ban in India</span></h3>
<p>On 3 April 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Madras_High_Court" title="Madras High Court">Madras High Court</a> while hearing a <a href="/wiki/Public_interest_litigation_in_India" title="Public interest litigation in India">PIL</a> had asked the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> to ban the app, citing that it "encourages pornography". The court also noted that children using the app were at risk of being targeted by sexual predators. The court further asked broadcast media not to telecast any of those videos from the app. The spokesperson for TikTok stated that they were abiding by local laws and were awaiting the copy of the court order before they take action.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> On 17 April, both Google and Apple removed TikTok from Google Play and the App Store.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> As the court refused to reconsider the ban, the company stated that they had removed over 6 million videos that violated their content policy and guidelines.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 April 2019, the ban was lifted after a court in Tamil Nadu reversed its order of prohibiting downloads of the app from the App Store and Google Play, following a plea from TikTok developer Bytedance Technology.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> India's TikTok ban might have cost the app 15 million new users.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_transfer_class_action_lawsuit">Data transfer class action lawsuit</span></h3>
<p>In November 2019, a <a href="/wiki/Class_action" title="Class action">class action</a> lawsuit was filed in California that alleged that TikTok transferred personally-identifiable information of U.S. persons to servers located in China owned by Tencent and <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fatalities_caused_by_TikTok">Fatalities caused by TikTok</span></h3>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=TikTok&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22TikTok%22">"TikTok"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22TikTok%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22TikTok%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22TikTok%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22TikTok%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22TikTok%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2020</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There have been multiple TikTok related accidents that have resulted in users losing their lives or severely injuring themselves while filming. The most common types of TikToks that led to these deaths and injuries included stunts, challenges, weapons, vehicles, and suicides. Monitored by the website, "TikTok Death Tracker," an aggregator of news stories regarding these fatalities, these incidents have most commonly occurred in countries such as Australia, Pakistan, Canada, USA, Brazil, and Kuwait.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The most recent death on 11 March 2020, took place in India where a TikTok craze caused a newly married man to be crushed by tractor while performing a stunt in hopes to gain fame on the app. Cyberbullying via the ‘Comments’ section in TikTok can instigate the worsening of mental health issues, and cause self-harm and self-mutilation in susceptible individuals. The first death recorded on 19 October 2018, was in India as well where a Chennai youth male committed suicide from a vehicle due to being bullied for dressing up as a woman in his TikTok videos. The "TikTok Death Tracker" website was created to promote awareness of safety concerns to ensure users are being safe when posting and viewing content.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> TikTok claims to be a secure and safe app if users follow the terms and conditions that appear on a user's screen when creating an account.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The app discourages performing dangerous stunts or challenges. However, numerous participants have succumbed to the influence of popular trends and have completed viral challenges on the TikTok app. The TikTok creators developed a modification in the app's algorithm to ban certain hashtags such as ones that promote things such as eating disorders and self harming behaviors to cultivate a safe and healthy media environment. Not all of these trends appear outwardly dangerous at first glance. A trend referred to as the "nutmeg challenge" has recently gone viral with 46.4 million views under the hashtag on the app as of April 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The challenge involves the creator ingesting two to four tablespoons of <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> often in a beverage like water or milk. The high that may come alongside this is real, but can have devastating health consequences. According to the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_Clinical_Chemistry" title="American Association for Clinical Chemistry">American Association for Clinical Chemistry</a>, the consumption of the spice can result in not only hallucinations, but also agitation, hypothermia, numbness, blurred vision, nausea, dry mouth, coma, and death. TikTok released a public statement after the trend went viral noting, "the safety and well-being of our users is a top priority at TikTok. As we make clear in our Community Guidelines, we do not allow content that displays, promotes, or encourages drugs or drug consumption. We remove any such reported content." Some content may not be allowed to be uploaded if deemed inappropriate or against the terms and conditions. This restriction helps protect others from viewing disturbing content while scrolling through the main page.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
